# KOLM W920 — Frontier Audit & Verified Fix-List

> Read-only audit of every kolm surface vs the SOTA frontier. Each finding was adversarially verified (refuted-by-default); only `isReal && !alreadyPresent` survive. Source workflow: `wf_9b491135-ed9` · 152 agents · 152 · generated 2026-05-29.

**96 verified findings** across 11 surfaces — 10 critical · 29 high · 44 medium · 13 low.

**Method:** Synthesized from 9 per-surface frontier scans + per-surface completeness audits + standalone refutation notes under audit/w920/. Effort/impact reflect adjudicated verdicts and refutations where they revised the raw finding. Read-only on product code; this is a plan, not a patch.

**Legend:** {"impact":"critical > high > medium > low (business/correctness leverage, adjusted for kolm's actual positioning)","effort_days":"engineering-days, adjusted to verdict where the verifier revised it","depends_on":"must land first (by item title or phase)"}

## Global notes

- Two themes dominate: (1) build-but-unwired modules — the biggest wins are integration, not invention (confidence-router W807, multi_lora.py, eagle3.py, disagg.py, distill-preference miner without trainer, adversarial-prompts classifier, ks-sparkline, account-shell precedent). (2) source-of-truth drift — route manifest/OpenAPI stale, two redaction surfaces, two docker/k8s emitters, two lifecycle transition tables, gate-name list in 3 places, pricing tiers in 3 places.
- Three live correctness/compliance bugs leak silently: gateway output redaction never reaches the client; gateway cost_usd defaults to $0 on estimator failure; fallback_reason/route_decision enum drift can throw mid-call and structurally zeroes drift+cost signals.
- Ship-gate is RED on the current tree (51/52) and default release:verify FAILS — three test-only fixes unblock the entire gate.
- REFUTED / already-present (do NOT build): CLI-verb behavioral smoke tests (110/665 files already do this); willArtifactFit reimplementation (the real gate is forge-fit.js and is shipped; willArtifactFit is dead code — delete it); witness-cosign anchoring (auditor-attestation.js + sigstore.js already deliver the buyer outcome). Unsloth/Liger fast path is mostly shipped (trainer_real.py) — residual is a packaging line + sample-packing only.
- DOWNGRADED by verdict: gateway semantic cache and prompt-injection wiring impact tempered for kolm's distill-first positioning; RouteLLM learned router high->medium (W807 entropy splice already captures much of the lever); social-proof critical->medium (no named customers, anonymization policy forbids the proposed remedy).

## Top leverage (highest-differentiation items)

1. **Unblock the RED ship-gate (wave214 slice + wave526 gate-count + provenance file)** _(tests-gate)_ — Every '52/52 green' claim is currently false; three test-only edits with zero product risk restore a truthful ship gate and turn the existing 665 tests back into a working net.
2. **Apply output redaction to the client response at /v1/gateway/dispatch** _(gateway)_ — redact_all/redact_captures customers receive un-redacted PII/PHI while the signed receipt claims redaction_applied — a HIPAA-grade leak on the flagship route. Few-line fix with an in-repo reference.
3. **Regenerate stale route manifest + OpenAPI + wire a --check drift gate** _(routes-api)_ — 55 shipped live routes / 9 groups (entire no-code wizard, fleet, autopilot data-engine) are absent from the public contract. 15-min regen is the root cause of 4 failing audit checks; the --check gate stops it recurring forever.
4. **Make no-code Compile produce a REAL signed .kolm (kill the 22-event stub)** _(account-ui)_ — The flagship no-code flow is UI-complete but delivers a fake artifact whose slug 404s; everything downstream (artifacts, verify, receipts) is already real, so a real job lights up the whole cockpit.
5. **Wire multi-LoRA serving (one base, N adapters) into serve.py + CLI + HTTP** _(run)_ — The single biggest serving economic differentiator (S-LoRA/Punica) is implemented in multi_lora.py but unreachable; kolm distills LoRA as a first-class output but can only serve one at a time — value leaks at the serve boundary.
6. **Coerce fallback_reason at the receipt boundary + fix frontier_fallback dead branches** _(govern)_ — A logging-field enum can throw and abort a live gateway call; separately the drift detector's headline signal and cost-report fallback bucket are structurally zeroed on real data. Few lines, two operator-facing outputs.
7. **Add logit-level KD loss (KL / DistiLLM-2) — the actual distillation objective** _(studio)_ — kolm markets 'distillation' but both trainers do plain SFT on teacher strings; the logit/SKL objective is what makes the K-score T-axis defensible and differentiates from generic SFT platforms.
8. **Anytime-valid A/B gate (mSPRT) + retention guard on the re-distill loop** _(autopilot)_ — The autopilot re-peeks a fixed-sample t-test every tick (invalid, inflates false promotes/rollbacks) and retrains every tick with no catastrophic-forgetting guard — the two correctness holes in the autonomous core, both buildable from primitives already in-repo.

## Phased execution sequence

**Phase 1: Phase 0 — Unblock the gate (RED -> GREEN), ~1.25d**
- tests-gate: wave214 source-slice fix
- tests-gate: wave526/wave529 gate-count fix + export GATE_NAMES
- tests-gate: regenerate w889 provenance file

**Phase 2: Phase 1 — Critical correctness/compliance bugs, ~5.5d**
- gateway: apply output redaction to client response
- govern: coerce fallback_reason at receipt boundary (logging can't crash a call)
- govern: fix frontier_fallback dead branches in drift+cost
- gateway: fix silent $0 cost (estimator_status + null)

**Phase 3: Phase 2 — Quick high-leverage wins (low effort, high impact), ~4d**
- routes-api: regenerate manifest+OpenAPI (0.25d) + add --check drift gate (0.5d)
- account-ui: define --good/--bad/--warn tokens in ks.css (0.5d)
- data-engine: request nomic embedder instead of hardcoded ngram (0.5d)
- website: single source of truth for pricing tiers + dead footer links
- routes-api: wire verify:surfaces + emit per-op OpenAPI security

**Phase 4: Phase 3 — Flagship credibility integrations (build-but-unwired), ~24d**
- account-ui: no-code Compile produces a REAL signed .kolm
- run: wire multi-LoRA serving into serve.py+CLI+HTTP
- studio: add logit-level KD loss (the real distillation objective)
- run: FP8 KV/prefix/lora/spec parity between serve and deploy
- run: EAGLE-3 head from artifact into serve.py
- studio: real SimPO/ORPO/KTO preference trainer

**Phase 5: Phase 4 — Autonomous-core correctness, ~12d**
- autopilot: anytime-valid mSPRT A/B gate
- autopilot: catastrophic-forgetting retention guard + replay
- autopilot: split-conformal prediction interval
- autopilot: canary/shadow window before EXECUTE (after mSPRT)

**Phase 6: Phase 5 — Trust/observability/standards depth, ~20d**
- govern: transparency-log anchor per-call receipts (after Merkle fix)
- govern: KMS/HSM signing
- govern: fix RFC 6962 verifier
- gateway: exact-hash + semantic cache
- gateway: gen_ai.* OTel semconv
- run: probe.py tested-passport path
- routes-api: real per-endpoint schemas + Spectral lint

**Phase 7: Phase 6 — DX, conversion, data-quality frontier, ongoing**
- cli-tui: dual-consumer error envelope + rejectUnknownFlags + dynamic completion
- account-ui: command palette + shared shell + sparkline rollout
- website: live playground + social proof + OSS-traction + final CTA
- data-engine: IFD difficulty + DEITA selection + Magpie + SemDeDup
- studio: GRPO + mergekit + Arena-Hard harness
- autopilot: Thompson bandit + learning-curve + contextual-bandit priors
- tests-gate: coverage floor + data-engine tests + mutation testing + SLSA provenance

## Findings by surface

### Tests & ship-gate  `tests-gate`

_9 verified findings (2 critical, 3 high)._

**Audit summary.** The Tests & ship-gate surface is real and well-structured, not a stub: scripts/ship-gate.cjs orchestrates 52 checks across 7 surfaces with a self-check that enforces counts/ids, and scripts/release-verify.cjs runs 13 gates with genuine per-gate semantic validation (not just 'did it emit JSON'). The orchestrator envelope/surface-count contracts are pinned by green smoke tests (wave888i 6/6, wave910 10/10). Two concrete failures exist on the current tree. (1) The live 52-check ship-gate exits 1 (51/52): check #32 fails because tests/wave214-distill-from-captures.test.js #10 slices only the first 2000 chars of cmdDistill() and W918's agent-mode insertion pushed the '--from-captures' dispatch past that window — the product code is correct (dispatch at cli/kolm.js:21587, function at 22119), this is a brittle-test regression. (2) release-verify lock-in wave526 #8 asserts exactly 12 gates but the driver now emits 13 (the ship-gate gate was added in W888-I without updating the test). Both reproduce in the 2026-05-29 full-suite log. Notable design property: several ship-gate checks (#15 GGUF, #26 k8s, #34 shard-KV, plus persona extensions) count environment SKIP as PASS, so a '52/52 green' on a bare CI box does not certify those GPU/kubectl-dependent deployment paths were exercised. Full audit JSON written to audit/w920/tests-gate.audit.json.

**Audit-flagged gaps:**
- BLOCKER (brittle test): tests/wave214-distill-from-captures.test.js #10 slices only the first 2000 chars of cmdDistill(); W918's agent-mode insertion pushed '--from-captures' past that window -> live ship-gate exits 1 (51/52) and wave889-11 umbrella invariant #4 (failed==0) is logically red. Product code is correct (dispatch at cli/kolm.js:21587). Fix: widen the slice (~3000 chars) or match the whole function body.
- BLOCKER (test/code drift): tests/wave526-release-verify-json-mode.test.js #8 hard-codes 12 advertised gates but release-verify now emits 13 (the W888-I ship-gate gate was added without updating the test). Add 'ship-gate' to allGates; also add the missing 'ship-gate'/'control-files'/'claim-verify' to wave529 #9 ALL_GATES which is currently an incomplete subset.
- DESIGN RISK: ship-gate counts environment SKIP as PASS for checks #15 (GGUF llama-cpp), #26 (k8s kubectl), #34 (shard-KV CUDA) and the e2e personas. A green '52/52' on a box without GPU/kubectl/llama-cpp does NOT prove those deployment surfaces work, and summary.passed does not distinguish genuine-PASS from skip-as-PASS.
- COVERAGE GAP: release-verify's default invocation skips the ship-gate orchestration entirely (opt-in --include-ship-gate). The 52-check server-boot/scaffold/HTTP-probe logic only runs when the operator passes the flag.
- STALE DOC: data/w889-11-gate-failures.json asserts 'ship_gate_result: 52/52 pass' / failures:[]; the live tree is 51/52. Regenerate or annotate with the wave214 #10 regression.
- OUT-OF-SCOPE (flagged): docs/research/ci-test-deploy-health-audit-2026-05-12.md deploy-config drift (Vercel->Railway proxy, Docker skipping build:sdk, stale GitHub compile action) was not re-verified in this pass; test-suite.yml now exists and partially addresses the 'CI does not run npm test' finding.

| 2 | high | 0.25 | release-verify gate-count lock-in (wave526 #8) drifted 12 vs 13 — add 'ship-gate' | C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/tests/wave526-release-verify-json-mode.test.js, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/tests/wave529-release-verify-lockin-suite-honesty.test.js, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/scripts/release-verify.cjs | Add 'ship-gate' to the allGates array in wave526 #8 (12→13). Separately, wave529 #9 ALL_GATES (tests/wave529-...:142-145) is a 10-gate subset that omits 'ship-gate', 'control-files', AND 'claim-verify' — it passes vacuously and locks in none of them; add all three. Best fix: have release-verify.cjs export a frozen GATE_NAMES constant and have both tests assert against it, killing this drift class. | CONFIRMED real and not refuted. Running `node --test tests/wave526-release-verify-json-mode.test.js` reproduces `AssertionError: 13 !== 12` at line 109. Root cause is exactly as described: scripts/release-verify.cjs gateShipGate (lines 681-683) always calls recordResult('ship-gate', ...) — when --include-ship-gate is off it records skipped:true/ok:true rather than not recording at all — so the --json summary always carries 13 gates (verified empirically: lint:refs, control-files, openapi-sync, claim-verify, sdk-manifest, test, sdk-smoke, local-surfaces, ship-gate, doctor, whoami, verify-claims, billing-tiers). The wave526 #8 allGates array (lines 92-96) lists only 12 names (no 'ship-gate'), and line 109 asserts parsed.gates.length === allGates.length, hence 13 !== 12. No GATE_NAMES/ALL_GATES export or module.exports exists in the driver, so the proposed single-source-of-truth fix is genuinely absent and the gate list is duplicated across driver + two tests.  Corrections to the finding: (a) The secondary claim that wave529 #9's 10-gate ALL_GATES (lines 142-145) 'passes vacuously and locks in none of [ship-gate, control-files, claim-verify]' is partially overstated — I concatenated the actual wave529 SUITE files and all three substrings ARE present (control-files/claim-verify in wave526, ship-gate in wave528), so W529 #9 would still pass even with them added. The true weakness is that W529 #9 is only a substring-presence scan (not a real enumeration/count lock-in) and its list is stale at 10; the 'single exported constant' recommendation remains the correct fix, but the 'locks in none of them' framing is inaccurate. (b) Effort: the minimal red-fix (12→13 in wave526) is minutes; the full frozen-GATE_NAMES refactor (with CJS→ESM interop caveat, and noting wave529 #9 scans source text not a runtime import) is a few hours — 0.5 days is a generous ceiling. (c) Impact 'critical' is overblown: it is a test-only lock-in drift with zero product/user-facing behavior affected; no kolm end user sees it. It IS, however, a true blocker for a green release-verify run (it fails the suite, which fails the driver's own 'test' gate), so under the repo's '100% green before ship' mandate the maintainer must fix it. Realistic impact: medium-high, not critical. |
| 3 | high | 1 | Distinguish genuine-PASS from skip-as-PASS so a green 52/52 stops over-claiming | C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/scripts/ship-gate.cjs | In ship-gate.cjs track a distinct `skipped_as_pass` counter alongside passed/failed/not_yet; print it in the JSON envelope and human summary (e.g. '48 ran-green, 4 skipped-as-pass'). Add a `--strict` / KOLM_SHIP_GATE_STRICT=1 mode that treats skip-as-pass as non-green (exit 2) for the release box that DOES have the deps, so production gating sees whether GGUF/k8s/shard-KV actually ran. Keep default lenient for dev boxes. | CONFIRMED, not refuted. The code matches the finding exactly.  (1) ship-gate.cjs:318-326 — runScaffold returns ok:true when env.skipped===true, with the comment "SKIP counts as PASS per W888-L exit contract." The driver loop (line 740) does `if (row.ok) { passed++; }`, so a runtime SKIP is indistinguishable from a genuine pass in the `passed` counter.  (2) The named scaffolds skip exactly as described: gguf-llama-cpp-roundtrip.cjs (line 33-35) emits `{ok:false, skipped:true}` exit 0 when KOLM_GGUF_PATH unset or llama-cpp-python not importable; k8s-manifest-dry-run.cjs (line 51) and shard-kv-vram.cjs (line 30-45) do the same on missing kubectl / no CUDA torch. So on a bare CI box, checks #15/#26/#34 all report PASS via SKIP and roll into summary.passed.  (3) No existing implementation of the proposal. Grep for skipped_as_pass / KOLM_SHIP_GATE_STRICT / --strict / skip_as_pass returns zero matches in ship-gate.cjs. There is a `skipped` counter (summary, line 705/756) but it ONLY counts checks excluded via the --skip= CLI flag (line 710-718) — runtime env.skipped SKIPs never reach it; they are folded into `passed`. The two are conflated in naming but operationally distinct, which actually strengthens the finding: there is genuinely NO counter for scaffold skip-as-pass.  (4) The over-claim propagates upward: release-verify.cjs:709-716 reads parsed.passed directly and reports `${passed}/${total} passed`, never surfacing how many of those were runtime skips. So "52/52 green" in the release runner does not certify the GPU/k8s/llama-cpp deployment paths executed.  (5) Caveats on the finding's specifics: - The finding says "persona e2e extensions" report PASS via SKIP — partially imprecise. The e2e extensions (KOLM_SHIP_GATE_INCLUDE_E2E=1, line 676-700) are opt-in and append additional check IDs; whether they skip-as-pass depends on those extension files (not read here). The core 4 checks (#15/#26/#34 plus #38/#39/#48 which are also runScaffold-based) are the solid cases. - Effort 1 day is realistic and arguably generous: adding a `skipped_as_pass` counter (~10 lines: tag the row in runScaffold, increment a counter in the loop, add to summary + Markdown + human print) plus a --strict/KOLM_SHIP_GATE_STRICT mode that maps skip-as-pass to a non-green exit (~10 lines). The one non-trivial dependency is the smoke test (tests/wave888i-ship-gate-smoke.test.js) which hard-pins the envelope shape {total,passed,failed,not_yet,skipped} via --skip=1..52 assertions (lines 52-56) — adding a new counter key is additive and won't break those assertions (they check specific keys, not exhaustive shape), but a thorough change should add a lock-in assertion there too. Half a day to a day total. - Impact "high" is fair but borderline. This is the project's FINAL ship gate and the value prop is verifiable receipts/proof, so a deployment-path regression shipping behind a green 52/52 is a real certification gap that contradicts the product's own "the receipt is the proof" thesis. Users running production gating would care; dev-box users would not notice (proposed --strict keeps default lenient, which is the right call). I'd call it medium-high — accurate, low-risk, cheap, and directly aligned with the product's truthfulness positioning. |
| 4 | medium | 3.5 | Wire branch/function coverage with node's built-in runner and ratchet a floor in CI | C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/.github/workflows/test-suite.yml, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/package.json | Add a coverage step to test-suite.yml using node's built-in coverage (Node 20, no new dep): `node --test --experimental-test-coverage --test-coverage-functions=NN --test-coverage-branches=NN tests/`. Measure current reality, set the threshold ~5% below it, add a quarterly ratchet, emit lcov for PR comments, and gate the build on the threshold. Add an npm `test:coverage` script. | VERIFIED, NOT REFUTED (with caveats). Current-state claims check out against the actual code: package.json:84 `test` = `node --test --test-concurrency=1 tests/*.test.js` with no coverage flags; .github/workflows/test-suite.yml runs `node --test tests/` with no coverage step; no c8/nyc/--experimental-test-coverage/lcov anywhere in the toolchain (the only "coverage" hits are HTML prose and tests/wave485-openapi-coverage.test.js, which is API-route doc coverage, not code coverage). scripts/release-verify.cjs and ship-gate.cjs gate on "fail 0" and presence of named test files, never on executed code paths. engines.node>=20 (local v24), so Node built-in coverage is available with zero new dep. The named modules exist with ~stated LOC (src/data-curate.js 396, data-augment.js 456, data-evaluate.js 442, data-feedback.js 373, pii-redactor.js 205, gateway-router.js 366, gateway-receipt.js 182) and the data-engine four have NO test references at all (no unit test, and product-surfaces.json smoke probes do not touch curate/augment/evaluate/feedback) — so "never runs" is literally true for those.  Two caveats temper the finding. (1) Impact is overstated as "high"; it's a maintainer-facing quality gate. gateway-router/gateway-receipt DO get incidental integration execution (tests/wave888i-gateway-overhead.test.js + router dynamic imports), so the "13% of src never runs / flying blind" framing is partly overstated — basename-scan flags them as untested but they execute indirectly. kolm's actual users (compiling/running .kolm artifacts) don't care about internal coverage numbers. Downgrade to medium.  (2) Effort 2 days is optimistic and there's a material unstated prerequisite: kolm's tests heavily spawn subprocesses (release-verify boots `node server.js`; many tests run `cli/kolm.js` and server child processes), and the data-engine/router modules are loaded via dynamic `import()` *inside the server subprocess* (src/router.js:23797-23862, 6085, 6212). Node's `--experimental-test-coverage` only instruments modules loaded in the main test process, so it would NOT count subprocess-executed code and would report misleadingly low numbers — exactly for the data-engine/router code the finding wants to illuminate. Trustworthy numbers require NODE_V8_COVERAGE + c8 merge across subprocesses, which is more than "a CI line," pushing effort to ~3-4 days. Adjusted: real upgrade, not present, medium impact, ~3.5 days. |

| 6 | medium | 1.5 | Make ship-gate part of default release-verify (or a dedicated CI job), not opt-in-and-forgotten | C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/.github/workflows/test-suite.yml, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/scripts/release-verify.cjs | Add a CI job (or a second job in test-suite.yml) that runs `node scripts/ship-gate.cjs --json` on every push to main with the deps the release box has, surfacing the new skipped_as_pass count. Keep --include-ship-gate as the dev escape hatch but ensure the orchestration runs automatically on the path to ship. Cloud-key checks stay behind the SKIP envelope so the job stays green without secrets. | COULD NOT REFUTE — the finding holds against the actual code. Every factual claim verified: release-verify.cjs:683 (`if (!includeShipGate) return recordResult('ship-gate', true, { skipped: true, detail: 'opt-in via --include-ship-gate' })`) short-circuits the gate to skipped by default; the flag is set at line 81 (`includeShipGate = args.includes('--include-ship-gate')`). The orchestration logic the finding cites is genuinely real and lives ONLY in scripts/ship-gate.cjs, not in the *.test.js files: shared-server boot/reuse/respawn (lines 121-250), live HTTP probes (line 256), and the scaffold runner (lines 297-318). `node --test tests/*.test.js` (what package.json:84 "test" runs, and what test-suite.yml runs) exercises the underlying behavioral assertions but NOT this orchestrator wiring. Verdict: real gap (mutation testing genuinely absent) but the rationale mis-diagnoses which tests are weak and the impact/scope are inflated. |

### Routes & API surface  `routes-api`

_9 verified findings (2 critical, 2 high)._

**Audit summary.** The Routes & API surface is well-architected as a generated pipeline: src/router.js (~721 literal routes via buildRouter) -> scripts/build-api-ref.cjs -> public/docs/api-routes.json (736 routes, 193 groups, regex+array-expansion aware) -> scripts/build-openapi.cjs -> valid public/openapi.json (733 ops, security schemes, shared responses, curated-op preservation). Generation, stub-honesty partitioning, and build hygiene are genuinely solid. The core problem is staleness plus a verification blind spot: the W910 omnibus (router.js touched 2026-05-28) added ~55 live production routes (groups, fleet, runpod integrations, deploy, compile/estimate, target-profiles, gateway/health, notifications/settings, connectors/notify, etc.) but the manifest, openapi.json, and api.html were never regenerated (committed 2026-05-27). Those 55 routes are absent from openapi.json, absent from /docs/api, and entirely escape the product-surface ownership gate because their groups don't exist in the stale manifest. The openapi-sync release gate and wave485 test pass green because they only diff the two stale generated artifacts against each other and never re-derive from source. Secondary debt: the spec is broad-but-shallow (351/354 mutating ops use a permissive GenericRequest body, 152 ops are source-indexed shells) and declares no per-operation auth despite defining security schemes. The task-named path public/api-routes.json does not exist (actual: public/docs/api-routes.json). Full results: C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/audit/w920/routes-api.audit.json

**Audit-flagged gaps:**
- STALE MANIFEST (primary): public/docs/api-routes.json, public/openapi.json, and public/docs/api.html were last generated before the W910 omnibus (router.js modified 2026-05-28; manifest committed 2026-05-27). 55 live production routes are undocumented in BOTH the API reference and openapi.json. Fix = re-run `node scripts/build-api-ref.cjs` then `node scripts/build-openapi.cjs` (could not run here — would write product files outside the read-only boundary).
- Undocumented families with confirmed live handlers in src/router.js: groups (CRUD :17000-17058), fleet (status/deploy/rollback/stop/monitor :19344-19413), integrations/runpod (:19467-19512), deploy/runpod (:19521-19597), target-profiles (:3433-3441), gateway/health (:5774), account/next-actions (:14954), notifications/settings+test-channel+log (:14980+), connectors/notify (:1387), compile/estimate\|preview\|start\|stream (:1326+), devices/add\|remove, draft/save, playground/proxy, capture/snippet\|export.
- VERIFICATION BLIND SPOT: the openapi-sync release gate (release-verify.cjs:433-461) and wave485 test only diff two generated JSONs against each other; nothing re-runs build-api-ref.cjs and diffs its output against the committed manifest, so source->manifest drift ships green. Recommend a gate that runs the (idempotent) generator into a temp dir and byte-diffs vs committed.
- SHALLOW CONTRACT: 351/354 mutating operations carry only the permissive GenericRequest body; 152/733 operations are source-indexed shells with generic summaries and envelope-only responses. The spec is an endpoint catalog, not a usable request/response contract.
- MISSING AUTH IN SPEC: openapi.json defines bearerAuth+apiKeyAuth securitySchemes but applies them on 0 operations with no global security; the public/authenticated split lives only in HTML prose.
- PATH-NAMING: the task (and likely other internal refs) name public/api-routes.json, which does not exist; the real file is public/docs/api-routes.json.

No deep blockers.  IMPACT: "high" is slightly overblown. The benefit is a correctness/completeness upgrade to the spec for future codegen/Postman/external consumers — real but medium, not high. The soft-auth nuance (PUBLIC_API routes still optionally read a key) means `security:[]` is technically a slight simplification of the actual behavior, though it correctly conveys "no key required."  Net: real gap, not implemented, low-risk to add. Adjusted impact medium, effort ~1 day. |

### Website / Marketing / Conversion (public/index.html, public/pricing.html, public/compare.html)  `website`

_7 verified findings (2 critical, 1 high)._

**Audit summary.** The three core marketing pages are content-rich, polished, and consistent on the central thesis (compile your workload into an owned .kolm, $0/token after compile, Apache-2.0 self-host). The dominant Conversion-surface defect is pricing incoherence: the homepage and /pricing disagree on the tier ladder (homepage omits the canonical Pro $49 tier), prices, gateway-call allotments, and /pricing contradicts itself on compile-credit counts; the /pricing JSON-LD offerCount also mismatches the visible tiers. Two footer/nav links are broken across pages (/contact, /about). Most CTA targets, comparison sub-pages, doc links, and structured data otherwise resolve correctly, and compare.html is notably honest (wrong-fit + competitor-credit sections). All interactive conversion JS (ROI calculators, speed-race demo, annual/currency toggles) is implemented but reviewed statically only — several numbers are illustrative/hardcoded (speed-race constants, $5k Enterprise payback) or diverge from their own prose. Full result written to C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/audit/w920/website.audit.json.

**Audit-flagged gaps:**
- Homepage pricing section is missing the canonical Pro $49 tier and uses different gateway-call caps than /pricing; pick one canonical tier set and mirror it on both pages.
- /pricing contradicts itself on compile credits (Free 1 vs 5, Team 50 vs 250 between tier cards and the editorial block).
- Two broken footer links: /contact (pricing.html + compare.html) and /about (index.html + pricing.html). Create the pages or repoint (homepage already uses /book-demo for Contact).
- /pricing JSON-LD Product AggregateOffer offerCount=4 contradicts the 6 enumerated offers and 6 visible tiers; rich-result validators will flag it.
- Indie $29 and Pro $49 both advertise 500k gateway calls on /pricing — only compile credits differ (10 vs 50), weakening the upsell.

### Autopilot / Autonomous Agent  `autopilot`

_10 verified findings (1 critical, 5 high)._

**Audit summary.** The Autopilot surface is broad and mostly real. The W775 daemon core (enable/disable/status/tick) and savings join are production-grade and well-tested (24 hermetic tests incl. HTTP-route integration, all green). The W720 self-improvement orchestrator + compareAndDecide gate, the W832 toy stump-GBM meta-trainer, and the W777/W822 A/B router each have dedicated passing tests (I ran the four wave suites: 73/73 green). The newer 'intelligence' layer the daemon composes - quality-predictor (qp-v1), compile-simulator (cs-v1), failure-analyst (fa-v1), cost-optimizer (co-v1), and the autopilot-lifecycle capstone tickAutopilotFull (apl-v1) - is fully wired into HTTP routes and the CLI and behaves correctly under my smoke tests, but has NO automated test coverage (no test references predictKScore/simulateCompile/analyzeFailures/rankStrategies/tickAutopilotFull). Honesty contracts are strong throughout: cold-start heuristic predictor with LOW capped confidence, propose-only-default deploy guardrail (5 conditions + 48h grace), drift-red holds, and tenant fences everywhere. Top risks: (1) the autonomous-deploy guardrail is the highest blast-radius path and is untested; (2) the whole intelligence layer lacks a regression net; (3) the predictor is hand-calibrated to a single Trinity anchor and the GBM is deliberately a toy. Full result written to C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/audit/w920/autopilot.audit.json.

**Audit-flagged gaps:**
- NO automated test coverage for the autopilot 'intelligence layer': quality-predictor (predictKScore/backfillFromRuns), compile-simulator (simulateCompile/decideFromDeltaK), failure-analyst (analyzeFailures), cost-optimizer (rankStrategies), and the autopilot-lifecycle capstone (tickAutopilotFull/objectToDeploy). Grep of tests/ for these symbols returns nothing. All are HTTP- and CLI-wired and pass manual smoke tests, but no regression net exists.
- The auto-deploy guardrail (autopilot-lifecycle._evaluateDeploy) is the highest blast-radius path (can autonomously promote a model) and has zero automated tests for the 5-condition gate or the 48h grace/objection clock. The grace clock is intentionally test-backdatable (_eventTs prefers fb.proposed_at) but no test exercises it.
- quality-predictor heuristic calibration (CAL_SLOPE 0.92 / CAL_INTERCEPT 0.07) is hand-fit to a SINGLE real run (Trinity-500). Absolute K away from Trinity-like vectors is an acknowledged extrapolation; confidence is correctly capped LOW (<=0.45) but nothing validates it against a second anchor.
- The learned (GBM) prediction path has never been exercised end-to-end with >=1000 rows in any test; only the heuristic path is smoke-verified. The _toMetaFeatures proxy-slot projection is internally consistent but semantically arbitrary, so learned-path accuracy is unverified.
- kolm-meta-trainer is by design a toy depth-1 stump GBM with no regularization/subsampling; the documented production path (apps/trainer/meta_xgb.py worker shell) is referenced but not active - acceptable documented tech-debt, but the 'meta-distillation' headline is backed only by the toy today.
- cost-optimizer strategy feature-deltas are characteristic priors, not measured outcomes; ranking is only as calibrated as the heuristic predictor. Negative ΔK is clamped to 0, which can mask a strategy that would actually regress quality.
- bakeoff's real per-model path depends on KOLM_LLM_PROVIDER/KOLM_LLM_KEY; without them per-model contestants emit {error:'llm_not_configured'}. Coverage relies on opts.stubModel; real-LLM ranking accuracy is not asserted.

| 2 | medium | 4 | Quality predictor CI is a hand-drawn band, not a calibrated interval -- wrap predictKScore in split-conformal prediction for distribution-free coverage | src/quality-predictor.js, src/compile-simulator.js | Once backfillFromRuns has >= a few dozen (features -> observed K) rows, hold out a calibration split, compute the residual quantile \|observed - predicted\| at level 1-alpha, and return [pred - q, pred + q] as a conformal interval with real (e.g. 90%) marginal coverage. Falls back to the heuristic band below the calibration-size floor (same heuristic->learned flip pattern). ~40 lines of pure JS: sort residuals, take the ceil((n+1)(1-alpha))/n quantile. The ci band is logged/returned but does not gate any guardrail today. Conformal coverage is an asymptotic/exchangeability guarantee; at the finding's proposed "a few dozen" rows sourced from essentially one genuine run, the guarantee is largely vacuous and the calibration set is not exchangeable with future drifting autopilot runs. The finding invents a NEW calibration-size floor ("a few dozen") distinct from the 1000-row GBM floor, creating a third regime (heuristic / conformal-band / learned-GBM) the design must reconcile.  3. Net: a legitimate, well-sourced upgrade on a self-admitted fabricated band, correctly flagged as not-yet-present and partially-scaffolded — but it is a premature optimization on a cold-start surface with one real data point, and the interval it would calibrate is not currently consumed by any decision gate, so "high" impact is not warranted today. |

You cannot fit K(n) from the timeseries at all without joining to run features by run_id. The only paired (n_pairs, K) history is the meta-trainer backfill rows (_qp_features carrying n_pairs + observed.kscore), so the finding's data plan is half-wrong. 2. COLD-START FLOOR GUTS THE VALUE. MIN_ROWS_FOR_META defaults to 1000 (kolm-meta-trainer.js:61). The predictor itself only flips heuristic->learned at ~1000 runs. A 3-param power-law over noisy per-namespace (n,K) points needs many distinct n values; with the product's single measured anchor run (Trinity-500 ~410 pairs) and a cold-start posture, essentially every real user is far below any sane min-points floor, so forecast_pairs_to_target would silently fall back to the same heuristic. The 'biggest lever' delivers nothing for the users who actually exist today.  EFFORT: 4 days is low. The pure-JS least-squares fit is easy, but to actually deliver the proposal you must add a namespace field + thread it through TWO backfill paths (quality-predictor.backfillFromRuns and kscore-timeseries.backfillKScoreSeries), join n_pairs to K (timeseries has no n_pairs), gate behind a min-points floor, and re-wire _pairsSubScore to optionally consume a corpus curve WITHOUT breaking the calibrated Trinity cold-start anchor. Realistically ~7 days.  IMPACT: 'high / biggest lever' is overblown. It assumes mature per-namespace (n,K) history the product does not have for any user. For the cold-start majority it changes nothing; the existing Caveats in cost-optimizer.js already say to 'treat absolute deltaK as directional.' Real but low-priority; the genuine gap is the conceptual one (no extrapolation), not a near-shippable 4-day curve fit. |

That learns the (features->K) mapping from realized runs. So absolute K prediction DOES self-correct once ~1000 rows accumulate; what stays frozen is the per-strategy effect prior (how much a given strategy moves each feature). So before any posterior can be built you must first: (a) tag each run with the applied strategy, (b) capture realized base-K and realized post-run-K (requires a real run + eval to complete), (c) build the per-(tenant,namespace,strategy) posterior store with shrinkage-to-prior, (d) blend at rank time, (e) tests. Realistic effort is ~7-9 days given the missing data plumbing.  IMPACT (high) is OVERBLOWN. Realized delta-K accrues per (tenant, namespace, strategy) only when that exact strategy runs AND a candidate is evaluated — a very slow-growing n for any single corpus. For most users the posterior would sit at the cold-start prior for a long time (the finding itself concedes prior = n=0 default), so observable behavior change is rare in practice. Medium is the accurate impact. The diagnosis is correct and aligns with the autonomous-agent ideal, so users (especially the autonomous-autopilot persona) would care directionally, but the day-to-day payoff is modest until many runs accumulate. CAVEATS on the finding's own numbers: 1) Effort 5 days is optimistic. A real end-to-end build needs: the Python meta_xgb.py (train + held-out RMSE + serialized model), a new Node worker shell (spawn/doctor/honesty-on-missing/W786 envelope), wiring _predictLearned to prefer-worker-then-fall-back, AND a model-handoff contract (the JS infer path currently reads its OWN JSON model format; an XGBoost artifact is a different thing - the worker must either serve predictions or emit a JS-replayable model). The audit (autopilot.audit.json gap) also notes the ENTIRE learned path has zero automated test coverage today, so tests are net-new too. 5 days covers a happy-path shell, not the full tested path; realistic is higher. 2) Impact 'medium' is defensible but the practical product impact is LOW at current data volumes - the finding itself concedes 'the stump GBM is rarely even reached (n>=1000 rows)', and there are no rows.jsonl files anywhere, so no run has ever crossed the threshold even in tests. Every real autopilot decision today runs through the heuristic path (confidence capped LOW <=0.45), not the GBM. The audit explicitly classifies this as 'acceptable documented tech-debt, not a bug.' So the upgrade is correct and well-targeted (it's the right home for conformal residuals and removes the 'TOY' caveat) but is not urgent. 3) Unstated dependency: introduces a NEW heavy Python ML dependency the repo does not currently carry, plus the Python<->JS model artifact contract noted above.  Net: real upgrade, correctly framed as documented tech-debt with a named target path, lower-than-headline practical impact, effort underestimated. |
| 9 | medium | 10 | No cheap-proxy candidate screening before full compile -- add successive-halving (Hyperband/ASHA) over small-data trial runs | src/improvement-orchestrator.js, src/autopilot-lifecycle.js, src/cost-optimizer.js | When the cost-optimizer surfaces multiple plausible moves (or multiple student bases / recipes), run them as Hyperband/ASHA rungs: a small-budget trial (few hundred pairs, short LoRA) scored by the existing eval, early-stop the bottom half, escalate survivors to larger budgets, full-compile only the winner. The pipeline already supports pairs_override and partial runs; this is an orchestration loop in improvement-orchestrator reusing compareAndDecide for rung comparisons. Bounds wasted GPU on losing configs. | Could NOT refute the gap; the finding accurately describes kolm's actual code. compile-simulator.js (simulateCompile, L170-235) decides compile-vs-skip on a SINGLE proposed feature delta via two predictKScore point estimates; improvement-orchestrator.js orchestrateImprovement (L99-252) kicks exactly ONE distill config with student_base/use_curriculum/use_council/pairs_override taken from subOpts defaults (L151-154, 212-219); cost-optimizer.js rankStrategies (L282-310) ranks 5 strategies by predicted dK/dollar but ONLY as a forward projection through the heuristic quality predictor, not via real small-budget trial runs scored by eval; autopilot-lifecycle.js feeds the single recommended strategy delta to the simulator (L360-373). NOT already present: no successive-halving/Hyperband/ASHA/rung-escalation logic exists in src/ or tests/. The terms appear only in a wishlist research doc (docs/research/kolm-billion-dollar-distillation-lab-2026-05-24.md L41446, 85293-85295 -- arXiv links, unimplemented); 'rung' elsewhere is unrelated runtime-routing/multi-region failover ladders. The closest analog, quantize-bakeoff.js, runs candidate QUANTIZE profiles (not distill configs/recipes) and runs ALL candidates to full completion with a Pareto-frontier accept -- there is NO rung-based early-stop of the bottom half on a small budget then escalation -- so no partial credit. EFFORT: 7d is plausible-to-optimistic. The rung loop reusing compareAndDecide is a few days, but pairs_override only injects pairs into a single fire-and-forget run; there is no existing concurrent multi-config trial harness with poll/kill-loser/cancellation, pushing realistic effort to ~10d. IMPACT: medium is accurate but at the low end -- the author's own rationale concedes payoff only materializes with multiple competing configs/recipes, and kolm ships narrow Trinity-style recipes with effectively fixed config defaults, so this is a natural follow-on to a contextual-bandit cost-optimizer, not a day-one need. UNSTATED PREREQUISITES: (1) a low-variance eval trustworthy at few-hundred-pair budgets (the predictor is heuristic in cold-start, so small-slice scores may be noisy), (2) a concurrent multi-run job manager with cancellation (current orchestrateImprovement is explicitly single fire-and-forget non-blocking), (3) a real population of competing configs/recipes to screen, which the product does not yet generate. kolm's current narrow-recipe users would not feel this today; it pays off once multi-base/multi-recipe selection becomes a product surface. |
| 10 | medium | 14 | Ingest selection is a coarse +N-pairs prior -- add influence-based / forward-only data valuation to pick WHICH pairs to acquire | src/cost-optimizer.js, src/data-augment.js, src/quality-predictor.js | Add a lightweight forward-only data-valuation pass (For-Value style: per-pair score from hidden-representation alignment + prediction error using the current student in a single forward pass via the existing worker shell, no gradient back-prop) to rank candidate ingest pairs and prune low-influence ones before a compile. Surface a 'select-high-value' optimizer strategy (or refine 'ingest-more' to acquire top-k by influence) so the autopilot buys quality, not volume. Worker-shell task (apps/); JS side just ranks/filters the returned scores. | PARTIALLY REFUTED on premise, but the specific technique is genuinely not implemented.  VERIFIED-ACCURATE parts of the finding: - src/cost-optimizer.js:114-119: `ingest-more` really is a fixed coarse prior `delta:{n_pairs:+500}`, new_pairs:500. The module even self-admits (lines 54-56) the deltas are "characteristic priors per strategy, not measured outcomes of a specific corpus." - src/autopilot-lifecycle.js:101-121 `_deriveFeatures`: dup_fraction is computed by EXACT input-string equality (seen.has(input)) — exact-input-hash dedup only, no near-dup/semantic pruning. Features are aggregate counts (n_pairs, dup_fraction, teacher_diversity); coverage_score/avg_quality come from a curate run, not per-pair. - No influence-function / For-Value / forward-only hidden-representation valuation exists anywhere. The trainer worker (apps/trainer/*.py) has hidden-state access (embedding.py, moe.py use output_hidden_states/last_hidden_state) but nothing scores individual training pairs by influence on the student. So the proposed TECHNIQUE is real and not implemented.  OVERSTATED premise ("No per-pair value estimate"): kolm already ships a substantial per-example value-scoring + acquisition-selection stack the finding ignores: - src/capture-importance.js (W711): per-capture training-value score (token-density + entropy + MinHash novelty) driving WeightedRandomSampler oversampling. - src/active-learning.js (W815): scoreCaptureRichness (importance/weakness/novelty/recency) + detectCoverageGaps + recommendNextCaptures returns TOP-K acquisition targets ranked by gap_score x demand — i.e., it already picks WHICH data to acquire, and the autopilot daemon (src/autopilot-daemon.js:41,437) consumes getCoverageGapsForNamespace as its readiness/ingest signal. - src/active-learning-queue.js (W710): enqueues high-entropy/high-uncertainty routing decisions as the highest-value next-distill examples, priority-by-entropy. The existing selection is statistical (entropy/Jaccard/MinHash/TF-IDF), NOT model-influence-based — so the finding's specific For-Value forward-pass valuation is the novel delta, but its claim that data is treated as aggregate counts with no per-pair value estimate is materially incomplete.  EFFORT: 9 days is optimistic. A real For-Value pass needs to load the current student on GPU in the worker shell, compute per-pair hidden-rep alignment + prediction error over a candidate pool, cross the JS<->GPU-worker boundary with a new task type, return + rank/filter scores JS-side, add the select-high-value optimizer strategy, wire cost, honest envelopes, and tests. Realistically ~14 days, not 9.  IMPACT: medium is fair (not overblown), but tempered by heavy overlap with the already-shipped active-learning stack (which already captures much of the cheap selection value) and by the dependency that the highest-fidelity variant requires a GPU forward pass over an actual student artifact, so it only helps once a student exists.  Net: isReal=true (technique not implemented), alreadyPresent=false for the influence-function technique itself, but reviewers should note kolm already has statistical per-example value scoring + top-k acquisition selection, so this is an incremental upgrade of a shipped capability rather than filling a hole. |

**Planned action items:**
- [critical, 3d] **Anytime-valid A/B gate (mSPRT) for continuous monitoring (BUG)** — The autopilot re-peeks a fixed-sample Welch t-test (stat-sig.js gate, DEFAULT_ALPHA=0.05) every tick -> type-I error compounds well above 5%, so it can auto-promote/rollback on noise. Add anytimeValidGate (mSPRT / normal-mixture confidence sequence) preferred when the caller is the autopilot; keep welchT for one-shot human analyses. Same incomplete-beta machinery already in stat-sig.js. _(src/stat-sig.js, src/ab-router.js, src/autopilot-lifecycle.js)_
- [critical, 6d] **Catastrophic-forgetting retention guard + replay on the re-distill loop (GAP)** — (1) carry a small replay buffer of prior promoted-round pairs (SSR self-synthesized rehearsal) into each candidate set; (2) add a frozen RETENTION holdout (prior round's eval) and make compareAndDecide/deploy guardrail fail-closed if retention K drops > epsilon, not just live regression-class count. Makes the loop monotone-or-hold. _(src/improvement-orchestrator.js, src/autopilot-lifecycle.js, src/distill-pipeline.js)_
- [high, 3d] **Split-conformal prediction interval for predictKScore (UPGRADE)** — Once backfillFromRuns has a few dozen (features->observed K) rows, hold out a calibration split, compute the residual quantile at 1-alpha, return [pred-q,pred+q] with real marginal coverage; fall back to the heuristic band below the floor (same heuristic->learned flip seam). Replaces the admittedly-fabricated band the compile/deploy gates ride. _(src/quality-predictor.js, src/compile-simulator.js)_
- [high, 4d] **Thompson-sampling bandit traffic allocation (FRONTIER)** — Optional bandit mode in the W777 router: Beta/Gaussian-on-kscore posterior per arm from recordOutcome, sample-and-route argmax; keep deterministic 50/50 as sticky default behind a per-test flag (existing 21 tests unaffected); epsilon floor so an unlucky arm isn't starved. Posterior also gives the guardrail a cleaner P(B best) than a peeked p-value. _(src/ab-router.js, src/stat-sig.js)_ · depends: Anytime-valid A/B gate (mSPRT) for continuous monitoring (BUG)
- [high, 4d] **Power-law learning-curve extrapolation for ingest budgeting (FRONTIER)** — Fit per-namespace K(n)=K_inf - a*n^-b (3-param LSQ) from kscore-timeseries + backfill rows; replace _pairsSubScore's universal constant with the corpus curve; add forecast_pairs_to_target so cost-optimizer prices 'ingest-more' against the actual marginal pairs and flags diminishing returns. Gate behind a min-points floor. _(src/quality-predictor.js, src/cost-optimizer.js, src/kscore-timeseries.js)_
- [high, 5d] **Online contextual-bandit update of cost-optimizer strategy priors (UPGRADE)** — Per (tenant,namespace,strategy) running posterior over realized ΔK (compareAndDecide/flywheel already produce candidate vs base K); blend frozen prior with observed (shrinkage when n small); recommend by posterior-sampled ΔK-per-dollar. Frozen prior stays the n=0 cold-start default. Closes the 'never learns which strategy worked' loop. _(src/cost-optimizer.js, src/autopilot-lifecycle.js, src/kscore-timeseries.js)_
- [high, 6d] **Canary/shadow-eval window before EXECUTE in the deploy guardrail (UPGRADE)** — Insert a canary stage between DEPLOY_PROPOSED and DEPLOY_EXECUTED: route a small live slice to the candidate (reuse the W777 router), record kscore/fallback outcomes, require the anytime-valid gate to confirm non-regression on LIVE traffic before EXECUTE. Turns the 48h passive timer into a monitored canary on the highest-blast-radius path. _(src/autopilot-lifecycle.js, src/ab-router.js, src/stat-sig.js)_ · depends: Anytime-valid A/B gate (mSPRT) for continuous monitoring (BUG)
- [medium, 4d] **Embedding failure clustering + teacher-closed corrective pairs (UPGRADE)** — Cluster failing items by embedding similarity (reuse drift-detect path) instead of hash bucket; for [NEEDS_CANONICAL_ANSWER] scaffolds optionally invoke the threaded teacher to synthesize the fix pair (budget/opt-in gated). Closes the EVALUATE->fix->TRAIN leg without a human; eval gate catches bad fixes. _(src/failure-analyst.js, src/data-augment.js)_
- [medium, 5d] **Promote toy stump-GBM meta-trainer to real worker-shell GBM (UPGRADE)** — Implement the already-named apps/trainer/meta_xgb.py (W786 worker-shell pattern): depth-3+ regularized GBM on rows.jsonl, write model + held-out RMSE so confidence is data-derived; quality-predictor learned path calls worker when available, falls back to JS stump. Pairs with conformal (GBM residuals feed calibration). _(src/kolm-meta-trainer.js, src/quality-predictor.js, apps/trainer/meta_xgb.py)_ · depends: Split-conformal prediction interval for predictKScore (UPGRADE)
- [medium, 7d] **Successive-halving (Hyperband/ASHA) candidate screening (FRONTIER)** — When multiple plausible configs/recipes exist, run them as ASHA rungs (small-budget trials scored by existing eval, early-stop bottom half, full-compile only the survivor); reuse pairs_override + compareAndDecide. Payoff only once there are competing configs. _(src/improvement-orchestrator.js, src/autopilot-lifecycle.js, src/cost-optimizer.js)_ · depends: Online contextual-bandit update of cost-optimizer strategy priors (UPGRADE)
- [medium, 9d] **Influence-based forward-only data valuation for ingest selection (FRONTIER)** — Forward-only per-pair value (For-Value style: hidden-rep alignment + prediction error, one forward pass via the worker shell) to rank/prune ingest candidates; new 'select-high-value' optimizer strategy buys quality not volume. Heavier (needs GPU forward pass), research-stage at LLM scale — flag as the next data frontier after the cheaper gates land. _(src/cost-optimizer.js, src/data-augment.js, src/quality-predictor.js)_ · depends: Power-law learning-curve extrapolation for ingest budgeting (FRONTIER)

### Gateway / Route & Capture  `gateway`

_10 verified findings (1 critical, 3 high)._

**Audit summary.** The Gateway / Route & Capture surface is largely production-wired and well-tested at the unit level (60/61 gateway tests; full passes on confidence/poisoning/lake/capture suites). The dispatch pipeline (auth -> input-PII-block -> route -> fallback-chain -> output-scan -> signed receipt -> capture) is real and integrated in router.js. Two concrete correctness gaps stand out: (1) redact_all/redact_captures OUTPUT redaction is computed but never applied to the client response on /v1/gateway/dispatch (input block mode works; the connectorProxy capture path redacts correctly, the dispatch route does not), and (2) the W807 streaming-entropy mid-response teacher-splice machinery is built and unit-tested but not wired into any HTTP route, so the gateway uses a simpler pre-scored-confidence selectRoute. Receipt signing, fail-closed connector proxy, tenant-fenced lake analytics, the 3-signal poisoning orchestrator, and per-tenant auth/rate-limit/quota are all solid. Remaining items are tech debt: dual redaction surfaces, synthetic SSE chunking, best-effort cost estimation defaulting to 0, and one docs brand-lock test failure. Full result written to C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/audit/w920/gateway.audit.json.

**Audit-flagged gaps:**
- BUG: /v1/gateway/dispatch never substitutes outputScan.output_text back into the client response — redact_all/redact_captures do NOT redact output returned to the caller at the dispatch route; only receipt.redaction_applied is populated. (router.js:6349/6471/6556). Input block mode and the separate connectorProxy capture path do redact correctly.
- W807 confidence-router (streaming entropy window + mid-response teacher splice + emitSpliceWeaknessSignal) is built and unit-tested but UNWIRED from any HTTP route; live gateway uses the simpler pre-scored-confidence selectRoute. Advertised mid-response splice/per-token telemetry is unreachable in production.
- Two parallel redaction implementations (standalone w240 service over phi-redactor vs inline pii-redactor.applyMode in dispatch); the standalone service is not invoked by the gateway pipeline — detector-drift risk.
- Gateway receipt cost_usd is best-effort (try/catch, defaults 0 on cost-estimator import/throw, router.js:6373-6383) — silent $0 cost when estimator unavailable.
- wave742 #13 failing: /docs/gateway-mode.html missing 'ks-footer' brand-lock token (docs/HTML lint, not core logic).
- Gateway 'streaming' re-chunks fully-assembled text into 80-char windows (router.js:6502-6505) rather than true upstream token streaming; adapter-native SSE is a noted follow-up.
- Geo-fence HTTP 451 enforcement lives in the signup route (out of audited file scope) — isGeoFenced helper verified, enforcement call site not re-verified.

This makes the 2-3 day estimate roughly fair-to-slightly-generous for code, but the receipt change has a hidden cost the finding understates: stamping injection_classes/injection_score into the SIGNED receipt means touching src/receipt-schema.js ALL_FIELDS + canonicalForSigning (the Ed25519-signed kolm-audit-1 schema, gateway-receipt.js:1-3) AND its lock-in tests, or else attaching it as a non-signed top-level field like latency_breakdown does (router.js:6398). The signed-schema route adds ~1 day for schema migration + test churn; the non-signed route is cheaper but weakens the 'receipt as proof' differentiator the rationale leans on. Net effort estimate of 3 days is realistic if they take the non-signed field path; closer to 4-5 if they put it in the signed canonical receipt. (2) Impact 'high' is slightly overblown for kolm's actual users - the heuristic is regex-only (router.js patterns at adversarial-prompts.js:252-275) and the module itself disclaims production-grade detection (comment lines 23-24); shipping it inline closes an OWASP-LLM01 checkbox and is a real differentiator on the receipt, but a regex guardrail is table-stakes-but-weak versus the Prompt-Guard-2 classifier the finding names for Phase 2. Adjusted to medium-high. (3) Unstated prerequisite: namespace create AND patch paths both need the new injection_mode field (router.js:21955 create + 21997 allowed-update list), and a false-positive escape valve is needed since block-mode on a noisy regex will reject legitimate prompts containing phrases like 'ignore previous'. Overall: real gap, low-risk to wire, but the receipt-signing dimension and regex-quality caveat temper the effort and impact. |
| 3 | high | 9 | No true upstream streaming - the gateway buffers the full response then re-chunks 80 chars at a time (synthetic TTFT) | C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/src/capture.js, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/src/gateway-router.js, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/src/router.js | Add a streaming forward path in the adapters that, when body.stream===true, returns an async iterator/ReadableStream over the upstream SSE instead of buffering. Thread it through dispatchWithFallback (stream first attempt; commit after first byte, fall back only on pre-first-byte error). Parse provider-native SSE per provider (OpenAI chat.completion.chunk vs Anthropic message_delta), forward chunks immediately, assemble full text in parallel for the post-stream signed receipt (the receipt-after-stream model already exists at 6508-6527). Keep the buffered re-chunk path as fallback. | CONFIRMED, not refuted. The code matches the finding precisely.  1) Buffer-then-rechunk is real. All three forwarders (forwardAnthropic/forwardOpenAI/forwardOpenRouter at src/capture.js:283-358) call _w_N_hardenedFetch with requireJson:true. hardenedFetch is the single chokepoint for all upstream POSTs (src/providers/_shared.js) and ALWAYS does `text = await res.text()` at line 243 — fully buffering the upstream body before returning. There is no getReader/ReadableStream/response.body streaming anywhere in the dispatch path. Even requireJson:false (line 244-248) still buffers via res.text() into {_raw}.  2) The synthetic SSE re-chunk is exactly as described. router.js:6449-6544 — the comment at 6455-6458 explicitly admits "adapter-native upstream-streaming is a follow-up that needs per-provider stream parsers." Line 6471 reads the already-complete `outputText`, lines 6502-6505 slice it into 80-char windows. The post-stream signed-receipt model already exists at 6508-6527 (kolm_receipt SSE event after the full text), exactly as the proposed_change notes.  3) gateway-router.js dispatchWithFallback -> dispatchToProvider (lines 89-272) has no streaming branch; it just awaits the buffered forwarder result. body.stream is not even forwarded upstream (the param shaper allowlists known fields), so the upstream is called non-streaming and kolm re-chunks the result.  4) The two streaming-contract.js consumers (router.js:2512 streamingCapabilities and :2518 normalizeStreamChunk on a client-supplied chunk) are descriptive catalog/normalizer endpoints — NOT an upstream SSE forwarder. capture-stream.js is the capture live-tail (browser/CLI watching the capture lake), unrelated to upstream LLM token streaming. docs/product-math-frontier.json:660 lists streaming as future "Add acceptance accounting to streaming" work and product-research-atlas.json treats streaming as a readiness item, confirming it is not shipped as true pass-through.  So alreadyPresent=false for the actual feature (true upstream streaming); already_partially_present=true in the original finding is accurate re the wire-format scaffolding + post-stream receipt.  Effort: 8 days is realistic to slightly light -> adjusted to 9. The hard parts are threading a stream through hardenedFetch, which is also the retry/timeout/malformed-JSON harness — streaming a body breaks the "retry on 429 after reading body" and "502 on unparseable JSON" semantics and the proposed "commit after first byte, fall back only pre-first-byte" requires re-architecting shouldFallback/dispatchWithFallback, plus per-provider SSE parsers (OpenAI chunk vs Anthropic event SSE vs OpenRouter vs Gemini native) plus parallel full-text assembly for the signed receipt.  Impact: high is defensible (kept). Synthetic TTFT makes the gateway strictly slower than calling the provider directly with streaming, which directly undermines kolm's wrapper-tax/latency receipt narrative. Mild caveat: kolm's core users care most about the distill/capture/audit-receipt path, so interactive chat-UI TTFT is somewhat secondary to its positioning — but the claim that current 'live' streaming gives zero TTFT benefit is factually correct and worth fixing. |
| 4 | medium | 18 | Routing is a pre-scored confidence NUMBER, not a learned/semantic router - leaving the RouteLLM cost lever on the table | C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/src/gateway-router.js, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/src/confidence-router.js, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/src/router.js, C:/Users/user/Desktop/kolmogorov-stack/src/lake.js | Ship a lightweight learned router that, given the prompt, predicts P(strong-model-needed) and sets the confidence input automatically when the caller doesn't supply one. Start with a calibrated logistic/embedding-similarity router (RouteLLM 'SW ranking' style) trained on the tenant's own captured win/loss pairs from the lake (fallback_reason + capture_eligible already provide labels). The two confidence routers that DO exist are a different mechanism and do not satisfy the finding: src/runtime-confidence-router.js (W709) and src/confidence-router.js (W807) both compute Shannon entropy from the STUDENT MODEL'S OWN token logprobs AFTER/DURING generation (post-hoc, token-level → mid-stream teacher splice). Adjustments: (1) Effort 10d is optimistic — a quality-preserving router needs a trained/calibrated classifier or embedding-similarity model, per-tenant calibration, label extraction from the lake, a held-out eval harness to prove it does not silently downgrade hard prompts, an inference path inside the hot dispatch loop (latency budget for the gateway), receipt-schema additions to record predicted score, and the route_decision:'auto' namespace plumbing — realistically ~15-25d, so 18. (2) Impact high→medium: the 85%-cost/95%-quality headline is RouteLLM's MT-Bench (GPT-4 vs Mixtral) benchmark, not kolm's distilled-student-vs-frontier setup; kolm's existing W807 mid-stream entropy splice already captures a large part of the same cost lever in its actual architecture, so the marginal gain of a pre-call prompt-router is unproven for the distill use case and carries genuine silent-downgrade risk. Users (cost-conscious gateway tenants) would care, but the finding overstates the lift relative to what already ships. |

Net: real gap, correctly not-present, but low impact for kolm's positioning and personas; this is a scale/rollout nicety, not a survival feature. |

### CLI / TUI / Developer Experience  `cli-tui`

_11 verified findings (1 critical, 3 high)._

**Audit summary.** The CLI is mature and substantially exceeds the 2026-05-14 baseline (28 verbs -> 150+ in the completion registry). Most of the top-10 SOTA gaps from that audit are now CLOSED: EXIT.* constants defined + used at 100+ call sites; shell completion for bash/zsh/fish; `kolm upgrade` (check-only) + `kolm update` (self-install) with --json/EXAMPLES; --json on doctor/what/next/whoami/org and many more; error-with-next-step wrapper (kolm-ux.js errorWithNextStep + kolm.js withErrorContext); Levenshtein suggestVerb 'did you mean' wired into dispatch default; rich per-command help (146 maybeHelp sites, 57 EXAMPLES sections, exit-code docs). Accessibility contract (NO_COLOR/NO_UNICODE/--plain/--no-color/TTY/KOLM_NO_PROGRESS) implemented and honored. Primary `kolm tui` is a 14-view alt-screen TUI (cmdTui) with vim-style nav and a non-TTY guard. Ran 71 CLI/TUI tests across 8 suites: all pass. Two real gaps remain: (1) unknown-FLAG rejection (rejectUnknownFlags) is wired into only ONE verb (cmdCompute), so bogus flags are silently ignored on ~150 commands (gap #10 mostly open); (2) cli/kolm-tui.mjs is orphaned legacy wave-122 code — not reachable from `kolm tui`, with a mock/stub inference path and an advertised-but-unwired `--cloud` flag.

**Audit-flagged gaps:**
- Unknown-FLAG rejection (rejectUnknownFlags, cli/kolm.js:29942) is wired into only 1 of ~150 verbs (cmdCompute, :31632). 2026-05-14 gap #10 remains mostly open: bogus/typoed flags are silently ignored on nearly every command (verified `kolm whoami --bogus-flag` runs clean). A pre-dispatch flag validator or per-verb allowlists would close it.
- `kolm compile "<task>" --dry-run` with no --data ignores --dry-run and runs the real cloud compile (observed POST /v1/compile failing no_seeds_provided instead of printing a plan). Dry-run is only honored on the data-ingestion/--target paths. Minor inconsistency vs the documented --dry-run contract.
- cli/kolm-tui.mjs is orphaned legacy (wave 122) dead code: not reachable from `kolm tui`, contains a mock/stub inference path, and advertises `kolm tui --cloud` -> /v1/wrap/verified that was never wired (the 'Wave 123 will wire it' TODO at line 265 is unfulfilled). Recommend deleting it or documenting it as a standalone `node cli/kolm-tui.mjs` toy. It is knowingly carried (kolm-ux.js header lists the trio as exempt CLI shims).
- ExperimentalWarning lines (SQLite/WASI) leak to stderr on Node 24 for some verbs — cosmetic, does not break --json on stdout, but noisy; could be suppressed with --no-warnings.
- cli/kolm.js is a 54,645-line / 2.4MB single file — maintainability/tech-debt concern (verb handlers, help registry, completion registry, and two embedded flag() helpers all in one module); not a behavioral defect.

| # | Impact | Eff(d) | Finding | Files | Change | Verify note |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | medium | 2.5 | Global error catch is text-only and ignores --json (dual-consumer gap) | cli/kolm.js | Detect --json (and KOLM_OUTPUT=json) in main(); in the global catch emit jsonErrorEnvelope({error,code,exit,hint,next}) to stdout instead of plain stderr text when JSON mode is on. Standardize the envelope on the KOLM_E_* code taxonomy already started (KOLM_E_ARTIFACT_NOT_FOUND etc.) and add a stable suggested_fix/next[] array on every throw path via withErrorContext. | VERIFIED REAL, could not refute the core claim. The global catch in main() at cli/kolm.js:47524-47530 does `console.error('error:', e.message)` + process.exit unconditionally, with no --json branch. A SECOND catch the finding missed — the NL pre-dispatch catch at cli/kolm.js:46636-46639 — has the identical plain-text behavior. main() already knows about --json (it checks process.argv.includes('--json') for the mutual-exclusion guard at line 46602), so honoring it in the catch is trivial. jsonErrorEnvelope() exists at cli/kolm.js:40876 with fields {ok,error,code,exit,hint,next}. Finding said wired into ~6 sites; actual grep count is 5 (lines 40903, 41034, 41051, 41134, 41151), all in the intent dispatcher (do/explain/eval). Critically, AGENT_GUIDE.md line 57 documents this as a STABLE CONTRACT for agents: "Every verb that supports --json returns { ok: true, ... } on success or this exact shape on failure." The runtime does not honor that promise on the fallback path, so the doc over-promises.  alreadyPresent=false: the envelope helper and the documented contract exist, but the GLOBAL wiring the finding asks for is absent. Confirmed by tests/wave353-agent-guide.test.js — every assertion only checks the GUIDE text mentions the fields, none verify the runtime emits JSON on error. No KOLM_OUTPUT env var exists anywhere in the repo (the proposed KOLM_OUTPUT=json detection is net-new, not "already started").  CAVEATS that temper the finding: 1. Impact "critical" is overblown -> adjusted to medium. High-traffic --json verbs (e.g. cmdWhoami at 5641) ALREADY self-handle their EXPECTED error paths with structured JSON (catching API failures internally, emitting {logged_in:false, error, error_code, error_type, hint}). So the documented common failure modes mostly already return JSON. The gap bites on UNEXPECTED throws that bubble to the global catch. Exit codes ARE honored on every path (EXIT.* preserved via withErrorContext), so an agent can still branch on exit status even when stderr is text. That meaningfully reduces "cannot branch on errors" severity. 2. The KOLM_E_* taxonomy is real but thin (~8 codes: KOLM_E_UNKNOWN, KOLM_E_DO_NO_INPUT, KOLM_E_ARTIFACT_NOT_FOUND, KOLM_E_LOAD_FAILED, KOLM_E_EVAL_FAILED, KOLM_E_BUNDLE_RUN_FAILED, KOLM_E_RUN_FAILED, KOLM_E_DUPLICATE_ID, KOLM_E_UNKNOWN_DEVICE) — scattered, no central registry. Standardizing it across "every throw path via withErrorContext" plus the existing ad-hoc per-verb shapes (error_code/error_type) is a contract-touching refactor, not a one-block change. 3. RFC 9457 fields (type/status/suggested_fix/code_actions[]) are NOT present; current envelope is {ok,error,code,exit,hint,next}. The richer envelope the finding proposes is partly net-new. 4. Effort: the narrow centralized fix (detect --json in BOTH catch blocks, emit jsonErrorEnvelope) is ~0.5 day. But the finding's stated full scope (standardize taxonomy on every throw, add suggested_fix/next[] everywhere, RFC 9457 shape) is realistically 2.5-3 days and risks divergence from the per-verb shapes already in the wild. 2 days is slightly optimistic for the full scope; adjusted to 2.5.  Net: a genuine dual-consumer gap that contradicts a documented stable contract; worth fixing, but medium (not critical) since exit codes and the popular-verb expected-error paths already give agents something to branch on. |
| 2 | medium | 3.5 | Shell completion is fully static; no dynamic completion of artifact IDs, namespaces, model/target names | cli/kolm.js | Add a hidden `kolm __complete <line>` that prints newline-delimited candidates; rewrite the bash/zsh/fish emitters to delegate to it for arg positions (after inspect/run/fix complete *.kolm in ~/.kolm/artifacts and cwd; after --target complete the export enum; after --namespace complete known namespaces). Keep current static fallback when offline. | CONFIRMED REAL, NOT REFUTED. The current_state is fully accurate. emitBashCompletion (cli/kolm.js:33059), emitZshCompletion (:33088), and emitFishCompletion (:33121) all generate purely static scripts from the hardcoded COMPLETION_VERBS / COMPLETION_SUBS tables. Bash only handles COMP_CWORD 1 and 2 (verbatim: `if [ "$COMP_CWORD" -eq 1 ]` / `-eq 2`); zsh only CURRENT 2 and 3; fish only top-level verbs + second-level subcommands. cmdCompletion (:34817) and the dispatch table (:41295) have NO __complete entry. A repo-wide search for __complete / dynamicComplet / completeCandidates returns ZERO hits in product code (the only match is the audit finding file itself). So there is no dynamic value completion of artifact IDs, namespaces, --target enums, group slugs, or recipe names. NOT already implemented.  Caveats on the finding's own claims: (1) Effort is mildly optimistic. The finding asserts "kolm already has all the data," but that is only true for the verb/sub tables. The export --target enum (gguf \| onnx \| safetensors \| coreml \| mlx \| executorch \| tensorrt and quant tiers q4_k_m\|q5_k_m\|q8_0\|f16\|int4\|int8) lives scattered in help-text strings (cli/kolm.js:996-1021, 1471-1482), NOT a reusable constant — it must be extracted/centralized first. Combined with COMP_LINE/COMP_POINT parsing in bash, $words/$CURRENT handoff in zsh, fish commandline wiring, an offline static fallback, and tests across three shells, 3.5 days is more realistic than 3. (2) Impact is overblown as "high." kolm is a single-binary CLI, not gh/kubectl with thousands of users; artifacts live in one known dir and users typically juggle a handful. Dynamic value completion is a genuine DX polish item but not a value-unlocking gap or competitive blocker — medium. (3) Unstated dependencies: a __complete shim runs on every TAB, so kolm's CLI cold-start cost is a hard latency constraint; and the existing static-emit/install path is test-locked (tests/wave308-kolm-completion-install.test.js asserts idempotent eval-line install for bash/zsh), so any rewrite must preserve that contract. |
| 3 | medium | 5 | rejectUnknownFlags wired into only 1 of ~150 verbs — bogus flags silently ignored | cli/kolm.js | Define a per-verb ALLOWED_FLAGS map (or attach .allowedFlags to each cmd in the dispatch table) and call rejectUnknownFlags centrally from withErrorContext / _dispatchVerb. Start with high-traffic verbs (compile, run, distill, doctor, export, deploy, whoami, config) where a dropped flag is most damaging; global flags (--json/--no-color/--plain/--help/-h) are always allowed. | VERIFIED REAL, not already implemented. rejectUnknownFlags (cli/kolm.js:29942) is sound and does prefix-based 'did you mean', but has exactly ONE caller — cmdCompute at line 31632, whose own comment says it's 'proven first in cmdCompute' (audit gap #10). Confirmed by execution: `kolm whoami --bogus-flag` exits 0 silently; `kolm doctor --jsno` exits 0 silently (typo'd --json dropped); only `kolm compute pick --budjet 10` rejects correctly with 'did you mean --budget?'. The ~144-entry dispatch table (_dispatchVerb, line 41252) routes everything through withErrorContext (line 142) with zero flag validation. Two scattered partials don't cover the gap: `kolm hf modelcard` has its own ad-hoc rejection (line 54553) and cmdNl intentionally skips unknown flags (line 26637, by design for NL input).  EFFORT UNDERESTIMATED (3 -> 5 days): The proposal's premise that this is 'purely wiring + allow-list curation, centralized in the dispatcher' is the weak point. There is NO central flag registry — ~1076 inline flag reads (args.includes/flag()/pickFlag()) scattered across ~144 verbs and ~992 sub-verb branches. Flags differ per sub-verb (e.g. `group create` vs `group list`), so the _dispatchVerb choke point — which only receives (verb,args) — cannot validate without hand-curated per-SUB-verb allow-lists. 3 days covers maybe the 8 named high-traffic verbs (each of which still has sub-verbs); a real sweep is larger.  IMPACT SLIGHTLY OVERBLOWN (high -> medium): 'single most common CLI footgun' is rhetoric. The highest-damage verbs (compile/export/run) already fail on missing required positional args, catching some typos. But a dropped --dry-run/--json/--force on an otherwise-valid invocation genuinely yields wrong behavior with no signal — a legitimate medium-impact correctness/DX issue. Users would care for destructive/boolean flags specifically. |
| 4 | medium | 6 | No multi-step plan execution with per-step confirmation (Warp Agent-Mode pattern) | cli/kolm.js, src/intent.js | Add `kolm do --plan` (and TUI equivalent) that returns an ordered steps[] (each {command, why, destructive:bool}), prints the plan, then executes with [y/e/s/q] per step (auto-confirm read-only, always-prompt destructive). Reuse classifyIntent for each step; gate behind --yes for non-interactive and respect KOLM_NO_INTERACTIVE. Keep single-shot cmdDo as the default. | Finding is REAL and not refuted. Verified the current_state is accurate against actual code. cmdDo (cli/kolm.js:40895) classifies one phrase -> ONE verb via _dispatchVerb; --dry-run prints a single 'would run' line. cmdAssistantNlOneShot (12783) answers a question, surfaces backticked commands, offers only the FIRST valid command for y/N/e confirm — no chaining. cmdChat (29457) + chatPlanAction (27991) execute exactly ONE command per user turn ({action, argv, label, expensive}), with confirm gated on 'expensive' — per-turn single-command, not a decomposed ordered plan. There is no generic NL-goal -> ordered steps[] -> per-step approve/edit/skip -> read-output-and-self-correct scaffold anywhere.  NOT already present, but more partial scaffolding exists than the finding credits (so already_partially_present:true is correct): (a) src/intent.js WORKFLOWS + expandToWorkflow (lines 2004-2267) already encode ORDERED static recipes (cmd+why per step) for terminal verbs, surfaced for DISPLAY in /v1/free/chat (router.js:9560,9987) — but no destructive flag, no execution, no confirm loop; (b) `kolm quickstart` already has a per-step y/s/q confirm-or-skip loop with auto-skip of done steps + KOLM_NO_INTERACTIVE + --yes (HELP text lines 669-680) — but it walks a HARD-CODED 7/6-step wizard, not an NL-decomposed plan; (c) `kolm chat` already prints exact argv + confirms destructive/expensive commands + chatRunAction; (d) `compile --auto`/autopilot (7690,16681) is a guarded self-correcting loop (cost plan->simulate->deploy guardrail w/ 5-condition+48h grace) — but it is specific to the distill/compile data-engine, not arbitrary CLI steps. The genuinely missing piece is exactly what the proposed_change names: the planner (classifyIntent today is one-phrase->one-verb), the execute/confirm/iterate loop, and a per-step destructive classifier.  Effort 5d is roughly realistic — slightly optimistic. There is reusable scaffolding (quickstart's step loop, chat's confirm + chatRunAction, WORKFLOWS recipes, expensive-gating, KOLM_NO_INTERACTIVE/--yes conventions), which lowers cost, but the hard parts (NL goal -> ordered DEPENDENT steps where step 2 consumes step 1's output e.g. dataset_id; reliable read-output-and-self-correct since not all verbs emit machine-parseable JSON; a trustworthy per-verb destructive map) are non-trivial. Adjusted to ~6 days.  Impact 'high' is overblown. This is an opt-in CLI agent-mode tracking the 2026 frontier (Warp/Copilot CLI). kolm's actual users (ML/ops engineers + AI agents calling the CLI) are served first by the deterministic, auditable single-shot path that is the product's core differentiation; a bounded multi-step orchestrator is a credible-but-secondary nice-to-have and risks eroding the determinism story if built sloppily. Medium is more accurate. Unstated prerequisites: structured/JSON output from every step verb for the self-correct loop, a verb->destructiveness map (partially present via chat 'expensive' + server confirm_required), and cross-step argument dependency resolution. |
